Organizations</th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dedham_Historical_Society_and_Museum" title="Dedham Historical Society and Museum">Historical Society</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Society_in_Dedham_for_Apprehending_Horse_Thieves" title="The Society in Dedham for Apprehending Horse Thieves">Horse Thief Society</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/History_of_St._Mary%27s_Church_(Dedham,_Massachusetts)" title="History of St. Mary&#39;s Church (Dedham, Massachusetts)">St. Mary's Church</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dedham_Pottery" title="Dedham Pottery">Dedham Pottery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rust_Craft_Greeting_Card_Company" title="Rust Craft Greeting Card Company">Rust Craft</a></li></ul></td>
</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Dedham" title="Template:History of Dedham"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:History_of_Dedham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template talk:History of Dedham (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Dedham&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Dedham</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">DED</span>-əm</i></a> is a <a href="/wiki/New_England_town" title="New England town">town</a> in and the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County,_Massachusetts" title="Norfolk County, Massachusetts">Norfolk County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GR6_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR6-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The population was 24,729 at the 2010 census.<sup id="cite_ref-2010census_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010census-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It is located on <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>'s southwest border. On the northwest it is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Needham,_Massachusetts" title="Needham, Massachusetts">Needham</a>, on the southwest by <a href="/wiki/Westwood,_Massachusetts" title="Westwood, Massachusetts">Westwood</a>, and on the southeast by <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Massachusetts" title="Canton, Massachusetts">Canton</a>. The town was first settled by Europeans in 1635.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Dedham,_Massachusetts,_1635%E2%80%931792" title="History of Dedham, Massachusetts, 1635–1792">History of Dedham, Massachusetts, 1635–1792</a>; <a href="/wiki/History_of_Dedham,_Massachusetts,_1793%E2%80%931999" title="History of Dedham, Massachusetts, 1793–1999">History of Dedham, Massachusetts, 1793–1999</a>; <a href="/wiki/History_of_Dedham,_Massachusetts,_2000%E2%80%93present" title="History of Dedham, Massachusetts, 2000–present">History of Dedham, Massachusetts, 2000–present</a>; and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Dedham,_Massachusetts,_in_television_and_film" title="History of Dedham, Massachusetts, in television and film">History of Dedham, Massachusetts, in television and film</a></div>
<p>Settled in 1635 by people from Roxbury and Watertown, Dedham was incorporated in 1636. It became the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County,_Massachusetts" title="Norfolk County, Massachusetts">Norfolk County</a> when the county was formed from parts of <a href="/wiki/Suffolk_County,_Massachusetts" title="Suffolk County, Massachusetts">Suffolk County</a> on March 26, 1793. When the Town was originally incorporated, the residents wanted to name it "Contentment."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParr200911_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParr200911-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_General_Court" title="Massachusetts General Court">Massachusetts General Court</a> overruled them and named the town after <a href="/wiki/Dedham,_Essex" title="Dedham, Essex">Dedham, Essex</a> in England, where some of the original inhabitants were born.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParr200911_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParr200911-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  The boundaries of the town at the time stretched to the Rhode Island border.
</p><p>At the first public meeting on August 15, 1636, eighteen men signed the town covenant. They swore that they would "in the fear and reverence of our Almighty God, mutually and severally promise amongst ourselves and each to profess and practice one truth according to that most perfect rule, the foundation whereof is ever lasting love."
</p><p>They also agreed that "we shall by all means labor to keep off from us all such as are contrary minded, and receive only such unto us as may be probably of one heart with us, [and such] as that we either know or may well and truly be informed to walk in a peaceable conversation with all meekness of spirit, [this] for the edification of each other in the knowledge and faith of the Lord Jesus…" The covenant also stipulated that if differences were to arise between townsmen, they would seek arbitration for resolution and each would pay his fair share for the common good.
</p><p>In November 1798, <a href="/wiki/David_Brown_(Massachusetts)" title="David Brown (Massachusetts)">David Brown</a> led a group in Dedham protesting the federal government; they set up a <a href="/wiki/Liberty_pole" title="Liberty pole">liberty pole</a>, as people had before the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>. It carried the words, "No <a href="/wiki/Stamp_Act_1765" title="Stamp Act 1765">Stamp Act</a>, No <a href="/wiki/Alien_and_Sedition_Acts" title="Alien and Sedition Acts">Sedition Act</a>, No <a href="/wiki/Alien_and_Sedition_Acts" title="Alien and Sedition Acts">Alien Bills</a>, No Land Tax, downfall to the Tyrants of America; peace and retirement to the President; Long Live the Vice President," referring to then-President <a href="/wiki/John_Adams" title="John Adams">John Adams</a> and Vice President <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStone200464_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStone200464-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETise1998420_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETise1998420-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECurtis200088_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECurtis200088-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Brown was arrested in <a href="/wiki/Andover,_Massachusetts" title="Andover, Massachusetts">Andover</a> but because he could not afford the $4,000 bail, he was taken to <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Massachusetts" title="Salem, Massachusetts">Salem</a> for trial.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETise1998421_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETise1998421-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Brown was tried in June 1799.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStone200464_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStone200464-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Although he wanted to plead guilty, Justice <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Chase" title="Samuel Chase">Samuel Chase</a> urged him to name those who had helped him or subscribed to his writings in exchange for freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStone200464_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStone200464-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Brown refused, was fined $480,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETise1998_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETise1998-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimon200355_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimon200355-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and sentenced to eighteen months in prison. It was the most severe sentence up to then imposed under the <a href="/wiki/Alien_and_Sedition_Acts" title="Alien and Sedition Acts">Alien and Sedition Acts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStone200464_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStone200464-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETise1998421_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETise1998421-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dedham is home to the <a href="/wiki/Fairbanks_House_(Dedham,_Massachusetts)" title="Fairbanks House (Dedham, Massachusetts)">Fairbanks House</a>, the oldest surviving timber-frame house in the United States, scientifically dated to 1637. On January 1, 1643, by unanimous vote, Dedham  authorized the first taxpayer-funded <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public school (government funded)">public school</a>, "the seed of American education."<sup id="cite_ref-Sacchetti_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sacchetti-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Its first schoolmaster, Rev. <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Wheelock" title="Ralph Wheelock">Ralph Wheelock</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Clare_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Clare College">Clare College</a> graduate, was paid 20&#160;pounds annually to instruct the youth of the community. Descendants of these students would become presidents of <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>.
</p><p>The first man-made <a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">canal</a> in North America, <a href="/wiki/Mother_Brook" title="Mother Brook">Mother Brook</a>, was created in Dedham in 1639. It linked the <a href="/wiki/Charles_River" title="Charles River">Charles River</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Neponset_River" title="Neponset River">Neponset River</a>. Although both are slow-moving rivers, they are at different elevations. The difference in elevation made the canal's current swift enough to power several local mills.
</p><p>In 1818, though citizens were still taxed for the support of ministers and other "public teachers of religion," Dedham set a precedent toward the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state_in_the_United_States" title="Separation of church and state in the United States">separation of church and state</a>. Residents of the town selected a minister different than that chosen by the church members; the selection by residents was confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Supreme_Judicial_Court" title="Massachusetts Supreme Judicial Court">Supreme Judicial Court</a>. This decision increased support for the <a href="/wiki/Disestablishmentarianism" title="Disestablishmentarianism">disestablishment</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Congregationalism_in_the_United_States" title="Congregationalism in the United States">Congregational churches</a>.
</p><p>The local <a href="/wiki/Endicott_Estate" title="Endicott Estate">Endicott Estate</a> burned to the ground in 1904 after the local volunteer fire department, responding to three separate fires burning simultaneously, reached the Endicott fire last. By the time they arrived, only ashes remained. It is said that the estate's owner, Henry Bradford Endicott (also founder of the <a href="/wiki/Endicott_Johnson_Corporation" title="Endicott Johnson Corporation">Endicott Johnson Corporation</a>) took the burning of the homestead as a divine command to rebuild (which he did). The rebuilt Endicott Estate is listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>. The estate and surrounding grounds are open to the public, upholding Henry's stepdaughter Katherine's wish to use the house and property for "educational, civic, social and recreational purposes."
</p><p>In 1921, the historic <a href="/wiki/Sacco_and_Vanzetti" title="Sacco and Vanzetti">Sacco and Vanzetti</a> trial was held in the Norfolk County Courthouse in Dedham.<sup id="cite_ref-Bolton_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bolton-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dedham_Pottery" title="Dedham Pottery">Dedham Pottery</a> is a cherished class of antiques, characterized by a distinctive crackle glaze, blue-and-white color scheme, and a frequent motif of rabbits and other animals. Dedham is sometimes called the "mother of towns" because 14 present-day communities were included within its original broad borders.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dedham is located at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;params=42_14_40_N_71_9_55_W_type:city"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">42°14′40″N</span> <span class="longitude">71°9′55″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">42.24444°N 71.16528°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">42.24444; -71.16528</span></span></span></a></span> (42.244609, −71.165531).<sup id="cite_ref-GR1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> On the northeast corner of High Street and Court Street the U.S. Coast &amp; Geodetic Survey, now the <a href="/wiki/U.S._National_Geodetic_Survey" title="U.S. National Geodetic Survey">U.S. National Geodetic Survey</a>, has placed a small medallion into a granite block showing an elevation of <span class="nowrap">112.288&#160;feet</span>.
</p><p>Dedham is made up of a number of neighborhoods:
</p>
<ul><li>In the geographical center of town is <b>Oakdale</b>. It is roughly defined by East Street to the west, Cedar Street to the south and east, and Whiting Ave to the north.  The houses in the area around Woodleigh Road, which was declared to be one of the best streets in Greater Boston, have many homes designed by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bailey_Alden" title="Henry Bailey Alden">Henry Bailey Alden</a>, who also designed the <a href="/wiki/Endicott_Estate" title="Endicott Estate">Endicott Estate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-top_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>  Nearby the subdivision consisting of Morse Avenue, Fulton Street, and Edison Avenue, is named Whiting Park.<sup id="cite_ref-whiting_park_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whiting_park-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Riverdale</b> is an island surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Charles_River" title="Charles River">Charles River</a> and Long Ditch.</li>
<li><b>Greenlodge</b> runs along the axis of Greenlodge Street and the area between Greenlodge Street and East Street.</li>
<li><b>The Manor</b> comprises the neighborhood south of Sprague Street.</li>
<li><b>East Dedham</b> falls between Mother Brook and the <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> line.</li>
<li><b>Precinct One</b>, or <b>Upper Dedham</b>, is in the northwest corner of the town, between High Street and Common Street and the <a href="/wiki/Westwood,_Massachusetts" title="Westwood, Massachusetts">Westwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Needham,_Massachusetts" title="Needham, Massachusetts">Needham</a> lines.</li>
<li><b>Ashcroft</b> is the neighborhood between Cedar Street and Sprague Street.  It includes Paul Park and the Capen School.</li>
<li><b>Fairbanks</b> is the neighborhood between East Street and Wigwam Pond.</li></ul>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a>, the town has a total area of 10.6 square miles (27&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), of which 10.4 square miles (27&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 0.2 square miles (0.52&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) (1.79%) is water.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Massachusetts_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="List of Massachusetts locations by per capita income">List of Massachusetts locations by per capita income</a></div>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:left;clear:left;margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" id="cite_ref-1950_Census_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1950_Census-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1920_Census_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1920_Census-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1890_Census_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1890_Census-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1870_Census_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1870_Census-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1860_Census_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1860_Census-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1850_Census_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1850_Census-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>As of the census<sup id="cite_ref-GR2_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GR2-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> of 2000, there were 23,464 people, 8,654 households, and 6,144 families residing in the town. The population density was 2,244.6 people per square mile (866.9/km²). There were 8,908 housing units at an average density of 852.2 per square mile (329.1/km²). The racial makeup of the town was 94.51% <a href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="White (U.S. Census)">White</a>, 1.54% <a href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="African American (U.S. Census)">Black</a> or <a href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (United States Census)">African American</a>, 0.16% <a href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 1.87% <a href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>, 0.04% <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 0.80% from <a href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (United States Census)">other races</a>, and 1.08% from two or more races. 2.42% of the population were <a href="/wiki/Hispanics_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanics in the United States">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race.
</p><p>There are 8,654 households, of which 30.1% have children under the age of 18 living with them. 56.3% were married couples living together, 11.1% had a female householder with no husband present, and 29.0% were non-families. 23.9% of all households were made up of individuals and 10.4% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.61 and the average family size was 3.14.
</p><p>Dedham's population is spread out with 22.2% under the age of 18, 5.8% from 18 to 24, 31.1% from 25 to 44, 24.2% from 45 to 64, and 16.6% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 40 years. For every 100 females, there were 93.4 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 92.0 males.
</p><p>The median income for a household in the town was $61,699, and the median income for a family was $72,330. Males had a median income of $46,216 versus $35,682 for females. The per capita income for the town was $28,199. About 3.2% of families and 4.6% of the population were below the poverty line, including 3.9% of those under age 18 and 6.5% of those age 65 or over.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seal_and_flag">Seal and flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Seal and flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dedham_flag.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7b/Dedham_flag.JPG/250px-Dedham_flag.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/7b/Dedham_flag.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="293" data-file-height="216" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dedham_flag.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Town of Dedham's flag</div></div></div>
<p>The town's seal was originally designed by a member of the Dedham Historical Society.<sup id="cite_ref-norfolk_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norfolk-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  In the center is a crest containing the Old <a href="/wiki/Avery_Oak" title="Avery Oak">Avery Oak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-norfolk_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norfolk-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> When the tree was finally felled, the gavel used by the <a href="/wiki/Moderator_(town_official)" title="Moderator (town official)">Moderator</a> at <a href="/wiki/Town_Meeting" class="mw-redirect" title="Town Meeting">Town Meeting</a> was carved out of it.<sup id="cite_ref-DHSJan05_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHSJan05-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Above the tree are the scales of justice, representing Dedham as the county seat and home to <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County,_Massachusetts" title="Norfolk County, Massachusetts">Norfolk County</a>'s courts.<sup id="cite_ref-norfolk_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norfolk-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On the left of the tree are agricultural instruments, and on the right is a factory, showing Dedham's history first as a town of farmers and then as one with a number of mills and factories, particularly along <a href="/wiki/Mother_Brook" title="Mother Brook">Mother Brook</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-norfolk_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norfolk-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Below the tree is a banner with the word "Contentment," the name of the original plantation.<sup id="cite_ref-norfolk_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norfolk-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The town flag is red with the seal prominent and in the center. In the lower left corner is part of the <a href="/wiki/Avery_Oak" title="Avery Oak">Avery Oak</a>, and in the lower right is part of the <a href="/wiki/Fairbanks_House_(Dedham,_Massachusetts)" title="Fairbanks House (Dedham, Massachusetts)">Fairbanks House</a>. It hangs in the <a href="/wiki/Selectmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Selectmen">selectmen</a>'s chambers at town hall and in the Great Hall of the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_State_House" title="Massachusetts State House">Massachusetts State House</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A charter adopted in 1998 lays out the basic structure of the Town government, although it has been amended occasionally over the years. A seven-member Charter Advisory Committee, appointed in 2012, recommended six substantial changes and numerous minor changes be made to the document.  The Selectmen consolidated them into six articles for Town Meeting's consideration, and five were presented to the Meeting in 2013.  Voters approved four of them in 2014.  A version of the sixth and final proposal was adopted at the Spring 2014 Annual Town Meeting.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Town_Meeting">Town Meeting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Town Meeting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to Dedham's <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060525053420/http://dedham-ma.gov/index.cfm?pid=13072">Charter</a>, the "administration of all the fiscal, prudential, and municipal affairs of the town, with the government thereof, shall be vested in a legislative branch, to consist of a <a href="/wiki/Representative_town_meeting" title="Representative town meeting">representative town meeting</a>." Town Meeting is to consist of no less than 270 members, but not more than necessary to achieve an equal number coming from each precinct.  There are currently seven districts, but could be as few as six or as many as nine, with lines drawn by the Board of Selectmen and the Registrars of Voters every ten years.
</p><p>Votes are by voice unless members call for a standing or <a href="/wiki/Roll_call_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Roll call vote">roll call vote</a>, either of which can be called for by the Moderator. All Town officers are required to attend Town Meeting and multiple member bodies must send at least one representative who have all the privileges of a Member except the right to vote.  If 5% of Town voters petition the Board of Selectmen within 14 days of Town Meeting, any action taken may be submitted to voters. The final result is to be determined by majority vote, but Town Meeting can not be overruled unless 20% of registered voters participate.
</p><p>Town Meeting sets its own rules and keeps a journal of proceedings.  The Town Meeting may establish various ad-hoc and standing committees on which any Town Meeting Member or voter may serve.
</p><p>Before each Spring Annual Town Meeting, the <a href="/wiki/Public_Service_Recognition_Award" title="Public Service Recognition Award">Public Service Recognition Award</a> is given to recognize citizens who have performed outstanding acts of service to the community.<sup id="cite_ref-psrc_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psrc-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-new_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Town_Meeting_members">Town Meeting members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Town Meeting members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Currently Town Meeting consists of 273 members, or representatives, with each of the seven districts, or precincts, electing 39. Thirteen are elected from each precinct each year and serve a three-year term. Each precinct elects from its own members a Chairman, Vice Chairman, and Secretary.
</p><p>To be eligible, candidates must have 10 registered voters from their precinct sign nomination papers. Town Meeting Representatives can not serve on any other elected board or on the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Finance_(New_England)" title="Board of Finance (New England)">Finance and Warrant Committee</a>. Members who move from the district or are removed by <a href="/wiki/Redistricting" title="Redistricting">redistricting</a> may serve until the next Town Election; however, any member who moves out of the Town immediately ceases to be a Member.
</p><p>In case of a vacancy, the remaining term is to be filled at the next town election. If no election is to take place within 120 days of the vacancy, then the district chairman is to call together the members of the district, and they are to elect a member who will serve until the next town election.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Warrant">Warrant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Warrant">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Warrant at Town Meeting includes the articles to be voted on. Any elected or appointed board, committee, town officer, or any ten voters may place an article on the warrant. Each article to be voted on is directed by the Board of Selectmen to an appropriate board or committee to hear and provide the original motion at Town Meeting. All articles expending funds are directed to the Finance Committee; articles dealing with planning and zoning to the Planning Board; articles relating to by-laws to the By-Law Committee.  The Finance Committee recommendation has the force of the original motion on all articles except those related to zoning.  The Planning Board makes the original motion for those.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mini_Town_Meeting">Mini Town Meeting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mini Town Meeting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Chairmen of the several districts elect from amongst themselves a chairman. This Chairman of the Chairmen hosts what is officially known as the District Chairmen's Warrant Review Meeting, but is much more commonly referred to as Mini Town Meeting. The "Mini," first held in 1978, is generally a week or two before the actual Town Meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-mini_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mini-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The purpose of the Mini is to air out several of the contentious issues before bringing them to the floor of Town Meeting.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_Selectmen">Board of Selectmen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Board of Selectmen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The executive branch of the Town Government is "headed" by a Board of Selectmen.  The Board of Selectmen have five members who are elected for three-year terms and are the chief policy making body for the town. They appoint a Town Manager who runs the day-to-day affairs of the Town. They also appoint constables, registrars of voters and other election officers, the board of appeals, conservation commission, historic district commission, and members of several other multiple member boards.
</p><p>Selectmen set policy for all departments below it, but are not involved in the day-to-day affairs of the Town. They issue licenses and can investigate the affairs and the conduct of any town agency.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Town_Clerk">Town Clerk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Town Clerk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Elected Town Clerk serves a three-year term and works full-time for the Town. The Clerk is "the keeper of vital statistics of the town and the custodian of the town seal and all public records, administer[s] the oaths of office to all town officers... [and is] the clerk of the town meeting." In the role as clerk of town meeting, he notifies the public and members of the Town Meeting and keeps a verbatim record of proceedings. The current Town Clerk is Paul Munchbach.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Town_Moderator">Town Moderator</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Town Moderator">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Town Meetings are presided over by the Town Moderator, but he has no vote unless all the Members present and voting are equally divided. At the first Town Meeting following the annual town election, he is to appoint, subject to Town Meeting's confirmation, a Deputy Moderator from the elected Members. The Deputy serves in case of the Moderator's absence or disability. The current Town Moderator is Dan Driscoll.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_boards_and_committees">Other boards and committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other boards and committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The seven members of the School Committee are elected for three-year terms and appoint a Superintendent of Schools. They also set policy for the School Department. The School Committee is currently chaired by Stephen M. Bilafer, with Kevin R. Coughlin serving as Vice Chair. The other members of the committee are Mayanne MacDonald Briggs, Joshua Donati, Lisa Laprade, Melissa Pearrow, and Tracey White.<sup id="cite_ref-school_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The three elected members of the Board of Assessors serve three-year terms and annually make a fair cash valuation of all property within the town. The current chair of the board is Christopher J. Polito, with Richard J. Schoenfeld serving as Vice-Chair and Cheryl S. Sullivan serving as Clerk.
</p><p>The three elected members of the Board of Health are responsible for the formulation and enforcement of rules and regulations affecting the environment and the public health. Currently the board is chaired by Leanne Jasset, B.S.P. RPH, with Katherine M Reda R.N serving as Vice Chair. Mary P. Ellard also serves on the board.
</p><p>The Board of Library Trustees has five members, each of whom serves three-year terms, and has care of the Town's <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dedhamlibrary.org">public library at the Endicott Branch and Main Branch</a>. The Board is responsible for all library policy, the library budget, and hiring and firing the library director. The board is currently chaired by Margaret M. Connolly, with Sarah Santos serving as Vice Chair. Monika E. Wilkinson, Mary Ann Silwa, and Tracy L. Driscoll also serve on the board.
</p><p>The five elected members of the Planning Board make studies and prepare plans concerning the resources, possibilities, and needs of the town. It also prepares the Master Plan. Currently the board is chaired by John R. Bethoney, with James E. O'Brien IV serving as clerk. James McGrail, Jessica Porter, and Michael A. Podolski, Esq. are also members.
</p><p>There are five elected members of the Parks &amp; Recreation Commission. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ecode360.com/15734642">Section 3-10 of the Town Charter</a> states that the goal of the commission is to promote physical education, play, recreation, sport and other programs for people of all ages. The commission is currently chaired by Jon Briggs, with Tye Donahue serving as Vice Chair. Lisa Moran is the Commission's Secretary. Jim Maher and Chuck Dello Iacono are also members.
</p><p>There are five elected Commissioners of Trust Funds who manage and control all funds left, given, bequeathed, or devised to the town, and distribute the income in accordance with the terms of the respective trusts. The commission's Vice Chair is Ronald B. Slack. Bob Desmond, Emily Reynolds, Salvatore A Spada, and Dan John Oneil Jr. also serve on the Commission.
</p><p>There are five members of the Housing Authority Board. Four are elected by the Town and one is appointed by the Commonwealth Commissioner of Community Affairs. As members of the Board, they have all of the powers and duties which are given to housing authorities under the constitution and laws of the Commonwealth. The current Treasurer is Catherine Luna, with Donna M. Brown serving as Assistant Treasurer and Margaret Matthews serving as the State Appointee. Skye Annette Kessler and John B. Kane are also members.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The theater company and <a href="/wiki/Viacom_(2005%E2%80%93present)" title="Viacom (2005–present)">Viacom</a>/ <a href="/wiki/CBS_Corporation" title="CBS Corporation">CBS Corporation</a> parent <a href="/wiki/National_Amusements" title="National Amusements">National Amusements</a> is based in Dedham.
Dedham is also home to <a href="/wiki/The_Norfolk_%26_Dedham_Group" title="The Norfolk &amp; Dedham Group">The Norfolk &amp; Dedham Group</a>, a regional mutual insurance company.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_education">Public education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Public education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dedham_Public_Schools" title="Dedham Public Schools">Dedham Public Schools</a> operates seven schools and is known for the first implementation of a tax supported, free public school system, now used nationally.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dedham_High_School" title="Dedham High School">Dedham High School</a></li>
<li>Dedham Middle School</li>
<li>Avery Elementary School</li>
<li>Oakdale Elementary School</li>
<li>Greenlodge Elementary School</li>
<li>Riverdale Elementary School</li>
<li>Dr. Thomas J. Curren Early Childhood Education Center</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_education">Private education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Private education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition, there are several private schools in the town, including:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Noble_and_Greenough_School" title="Noble and Greenough School">Noble and Greenough School</a>, a private, co-educational day and boarding school for students in grades 7-12</li>
<li>Dedham Country Day School, a private, co-educational, day school for students in pre-kindergarten to eighth grade</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ursuline_Academy_(Dedham,_Massachusetts)" title="Ursuline Academy (Dedham, Massachusetts)">Ursuline Academy</a>, an independent college preparatory day school for young women in grades 7–12.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Rashi_School" title="Rashi School">Rashi School</a>, a Reform Jewish elementary and middle school.</li>
<li>Little Sprouts Early Education and Childcare, a preschool and kindergarten.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_schools">Former schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Former schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ames_Schoolhouse" title="Ames Schoolhouse">Ames School</a>, a former public elementary school named after distinguished Dedham resident <a href="/wiki/Fisher_Ames" title="Fisher Ames">Fisher Ames</a>.</li>
<li>Charles J. Capen School, operated from 1931-1981, now home to the Dr. Thomas J. Curren Early Childhood Education Center<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Church_(Dedham,_Massachusetts)" title="St. Mary&#39;s Church (Dedham, Massachusetts)">St. Mary of the Assumption School</a>, a former Catholic elementary school that operated as a part of St. Mary of the Assumption Parish until 1975.</li>
<li>The Quincy School, a former public elementary school that operated until 1982.</li>
<li>The Dexter School, a former public elementary school now operating as a private preschool and kindergarten, Little Sprouts Early Education and Childcare, Dedham location.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Apostles_Seminary" title="Queen of Apostles Seminary">Queen of Apostles Seminary</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Minor_seminary" title="Minor seminary">minor seminary</a> run by the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_African_Missions" title="Society of African Missions">Society of African Missions</a>, closed in the 1980s</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northeastern_University" title="Northeastern University">Northeastern University</a> Dedham Campus, a <a href="/wiki/Satellite_campus" title="Satellite campus">satellite campus</a> located in the Queen of Apostles Seminary's former building</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_of_worship">Places of worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Places of worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Boston United Hand in Hand Cemetery is located on Lower East Street straddling the <a href="/wiki/West_Roxbury" title="West Roxbury">West Roxbury</a> line. Dating back to 1875, the original plot was full by 1896 but subsequently expanded a number of times. There are graves as recent as 1980 in the West Roxbury portion; the Dedham portion is still active. Chestnut Hill's Congregation Mishka Tefila currently owns the property.<sup id="cite_ref-hand_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hand-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_organizations">Community organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Community organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dedham is home to a number of community organizations, including
</p>
<ul><li>The Dedham Combined Veterans Council</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/American_Legion" title="American Legion">American Legion</a> Post 18</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Disabled_American_Veterans" title="Disabled American Veterans">Disabled American Veterans</a> Chapter 42</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/USS_Jacob_Jones_(DD-61)" title="USS Jacob Jones (DD-61)">USS Jacob Jones (DD-61)</a> <a href="/wiki/Veterans_of_Foreign_Wars" title="Veterans of Foreign Wars">Veterans of Foreign Wars</a> Post 2017</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/AMVETS" title="AMVETS">AMVETS</a> Post 1636</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Knights_of_Columbus" title="Knights of Columbus">Knights of Columbus</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Rotary_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotary Club">Rotary Club</a></li>
<li>The Moose Club</li>
<li>The Italian – American Citizens Club of Dedham</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Boy_Scouts_of_America" title="Boy Scouts of America">Boy Scouts of America</a>
<ul><li>Troop 3 of the Boy Scouts of America was founded on March 5, 1917 by Charles H. Stackpole, a 52-year-old Methodist clergyman who served as the troop's first Scoutmaster.<sup id="cite_ref-troop_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-troop-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Peter Low was Scoutmaster.<sup id="cite_ref-troop_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-troop-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>  It is currently chartered at the Church of the Good Shepard in Oakdale Square.<sup id="cite_ref-troop_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-troop-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070605124529/http://dedhamlibrary.org/friends.htm">Friends of the Dedham Public Library</a></li>
<li>The Dedham Junior Women's Club</li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dedhamsquarecircle.com">Dedham Square Circle</a></li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dedhamcommunityhouse.org">Dedham Community House</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/James_Joyce_Ramble" title="James Joyce Ramble">James Joyce Ramble</a></li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dedhamhistorical.org">Dedham Historical Society</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Society_in_Dedham_for_Apprehending_Horse_Thieves" title="The Society in Dedham for Apprehending Horse Thieves">The Society in Dedham for Apprehending Horse Thieves</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Points_of_interest">Points of interest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Points of interest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fish_sculpture_at_Mill_Pond_Park.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Fish_sculpture_at_Mill_Pond_Park.png/220px-Fish_sculpture_at_Mill_Pond_Park.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Fish_sculpture_at_Mill_Pond_Park.png/330px-Fish_sculpture_at_Mill_Pond_Park.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Fish_sculpture_at_Mill_Pond_Park.png/440px-Fish_sculpture_at_Mill_Pond_Park.png 2x" data-file-width="3831" data-file-height="2567" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fish_sculpture_at_Mill_Pond_Park.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mill Pond Park</div></div></div>
<ul><li>The American Legion Post 18</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dedhamcountryday.org/">Dedham Country Day School</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dedhamhealth.com/">Dedham Health and Athletic Complex</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dedham_Historical_Society_and_Museum" title="Dedham Historical Society and Museum">Dedham Historical Society and Museum</a></li>
<li>Dedham Public Library</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dedham_Village_Historic_District" title="Dedham Village Historic District">Dedham Village Historic District</a></li>
<li>East Dedham Firehouse, possibly the oldest wood framed <a href="/wiki/Firehouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Firehouse">firehouse</a> in use in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-edf_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edf-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>  Originally built in 1855, it was designed with stables in the basement for the horses that carried the apparatus.<sup id="cite_ref-edf_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edf-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Endicott_Estate" title="Endicott Estate">Endicott Estate</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fairbanks_House_(Dedham,_Massachusetts)" title="Fairbanks House (Dedham, Massachusetts)">Fairbanks House</a></li>
<li>Legacy Place, outdoor shopping center.<sup id="cite_ref-legacy_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legacy-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MIT_Endicott_House" class="mw-redirect" title="MIT Endicott House">MIT Endicott House</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Moseley%E2%80%99s_on_the_Charles" class="mw-redirect" title="Moseley’s on the Charles">Moseley’s on the Charles</a>, the oldest continuous-running ballroom in the country</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mother_Brook" title="Mother Brook">Mother Brook</a> (first man-made waterway in the United States)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Noble_%26_Greenough_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Noble &amp; Greenough School">Noble &amp; Greenough School</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County_Correctional_Center" title="Norfolk County Correctional Center">Norfolk County Correctional Center</a>, situated in the median of <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Route_128" title="Massachusetts Route 128">Route 128</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County_Jail" title="Norfolk County Jail">Norfolk County Jail</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ursuline_Academy_(Dedham,_Massachusetts)" title="Ursuline Academy (Dedham, Massachusetts)">Ursuline Academy and Convent</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.vfwpost2017.com/">The USS Jacob Jones VFW Post 2017</a></li>
<li>Flag Day Parade: The Flag Day Parade began in 1967 and quickly became one of Dedham's most beloved traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-48th_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48th-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>  In 2017, for the 50th anniversary, the parade was moved from the traditional June 14, <a href="/wiki/Flag_Day_(United_States)" title="Flag Day (United States)">Flag Day</a>, to Saturday, June 17.<sup id="cite_ref-fireworks_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fireworks-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>  This was to accommodate the fireworks at Memorial Park that were part of the celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-fireworks_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fireworks-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Regional_rail" title="Regional rail">Commuter rail</a> service from <a href="/wiki/Boston_Massachusetts" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Massachusetts">Boston's</a> <a href="/wiki/South_Station" title="South Station">South Station</a> is provided by the <a href="/wiki/MBTA" class="mw-redirect" title="MBTA">MBTA</a> with stops at <a href="/wiki/Endicott_(MBTA_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Endicott (MBTA station)">Endicott</a> and
<a href="/wiki/Dedham_Corporate_Center_(MBTA_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dedham Corporate Center (MBTA station)">Dedham Corporate Center</a> on its <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Line" title="Franklin Line">Franklin Line</a>. Also <a href="/wiki/MBTA_Bus" title="MBTA Bus">MBTA Bus</a> route 34 Dedham Line to Forest Hills serves Washington Street. Bus route 34E Walpole Center to Forest Hills serves Washington Street, Dedham Square, and the Dedham Mall. Bus route 35 Dedham Mall to Forest Hills serves Washington Street.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Miscellaneous">Miscellaneous</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dedham,_Massachusetts&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Miscellaneous">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li><a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Ames" title="Nathaniel Ames">Nathaniel Ames</a>, almanac-maker and physician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Faxon_Atherton" title="Faxon Atherton">Faxon Atherton</a>, businessman and namesake of <a href="/wiki/Atherton,_California" title="Atherton, California">Atherton, California</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jason_Fairbanks" title="Jason Fairbanks">Jason Fairbanks</a>, murderer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Fairbanks" title="Jonathan Fairbanks">Jonathan Fairbanks</a>, builder of the <a href="/wiki/Fairbanks_House_(Dedham,_Massachusetts)" title="Fairbanks House (Dedham, Massachusetts)">Fairbanks House</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Temple_Grandin" title="Temple Grandin">Temple Grandin</a>, professor of animal science, inventor and autism advocate <sup id="cite_ref-grandin_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grandin-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_Haven" title="Samuel Haven">Samuel Haven</a>, archaeologist and anthropologist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eli_Sagan" title="Eli Sagan">Eli Sagan</a> (1927–2015), clothing manufacturer, lecturer and author in <a href="/wiki/Cultural_anthropology" title="Cultural anthropology">cultural anthropology</a> and political activist who served on the national finance committee for <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern_1972_presidential_campaign" title="George McGovern 1972 presidential campaign">George McGovern's 1972 presidential campaign</a>, a role that earned him a spot on <a href="/wiki/Nixon%27s_Enemies_List" title="Nixon&#39;s Enemies List">Richard Nixon's Enemies List</a> in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-Sagan_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sagan-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tommy_Vietor" title="Tommy Vietor">Tommy Vietor</a>, National Security Council spokesperson, podcast host of <i><a href="/wiki/Pod_Save_America" title="Pod Save America">Pod Save America</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
